			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Ford" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Ford_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Ford (disambiguation)">Ford (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;params=42_18_53_N_83_12_38_W_type:landmark"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">42°18′53″N</span> <span class="longitude">83°12′38″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">42.31472°N 83.21056°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">42.31472; -83.21056</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>

</p>
<p><b>Ford Motor Company</b>, commonly known as <b>Ford</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> automaker that has its main headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">Dearborn, Michigan</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> and incorporated on June 16, 1903. The company sells automobiles and commercial vehicles under the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_vehicles" title="List of Ford vehicles">Ford</a> brand, and most luxury cars under the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Motor_Company" title="Lincoln Motor Company">Lincoln</a> brand. Ford also owns Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Troller" class="mw-redirect" title="Troller">Troller</a>, an 8% stake in <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> of the United Kingdom and a 32% stake in <a href="/wiki/Jiangling_Motors" title="Jiangling Motors">Jiangling Motors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AR_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR-5">[5]</a></sup> It also has joint-ventures in China (<a href="/wiki/Changan_Ford" title="Changan Ford">Changan Ford</a>), Taiwan (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Lio_Ho" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Lio Ho">Ford Lio Ho</a>), Thailand (<a href="/wiki/AutoAlliance_Thailand" title="AutoAlliance Thailand">AutoAlliance Thailand</a>), Turkey (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Otosan" title="Ford Otosan">Ford Otosan</a>), and Russia (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Sollers" title="Ford Sollers">Ford Sollers</a>). The company is listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> and is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Ford_family_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford family tree">Ford family</a>; they have minority ownership but the majority of the voting power.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FordFamily_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FordFamily-4">[4]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption <ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Credit_Company" title="Ford Motor Credit Company">Ford Credit</a></li></ul><b>Other</b>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Automotive_Components_Holdings" title="Automotive Components Holdings">Automotive Components Holdings</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Getrag" class="mw-redirect" title="Getrag">Getrag</a> (50%)</li></ul><b>International</b>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Argentina" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Motor Company of Argentina">Ford of Argentina</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Canada" title="Ford Motor Company of Canada">Ford of Canada</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_India_Private_Limited" title="Ford India Private Limited">Ford of India</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Japan" title="Ford Motor Company of Japan">Ford of Japan</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company_of_Korea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford Motor Company of Korea (page does not exist)">Ford of Korea</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Motor Company of New Zealand">Ford of New Zealand</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford Motor Company of China (page does not exist)">Ford of China</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_Philippines" title="Ford Motor Company Philippines">Ford of Philippines</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company_of_Taiwan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford Motor Company of Taiwan (page does not exist)">Ford of Taiwan</a></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ford.com">ford<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Ford introduced methods for large-scale manufacturing of cars and large-scale management of an industrial workforce using elaborately engineered manufacturing sequences typified by moving <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly lines</a>; by 1914, these methods were known around the world as <a href="/wiki/Fordism" title="Fordism">Fordism</a>. Ford's former UK subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a>, acquired in 1989 and 2000 respectively, were sold to the Indian automaker <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> in March 2008. Ford owned the Swedish automaker <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo</a> from 1999 to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2011, Ford discontinued the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> brand, under which it had marketed entry-level luxury cars in the United States, Canada, Mexico, and the Middle East since 1938.
</p><p>Ford is the second-largest U.S.-based automaker (behind <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry#By_manufacturer" title="Automotive industry">fifth-largest</a> in the world (behind <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">VW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Group" title="Hyundai Motor Group">Hyundai-Kia</a> and General Motors) based on 2015 vehicle production. At the end of 2010, Ford was the fifth largest automaker in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The company went public in 1956 but the Ford family, through special Class B shares, still retain 40 percent voting rights.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FordFamily_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FordFamily-4">[4]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">the financial crisis</a> at the beginning of the 21st century, it was close to bankruptcy, but it has since returned to profitability.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Ford was the eleventh-ranked overall American-based company in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list, based on global revenues in 2017 of $156.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2008, Ford produced 5.532 million automobiles<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and employed about 213,000 employees at around 90 plants and facilities worldwide.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ford_Motor_Company" title="History of Ford Motor Company">History of Ford Motor Company</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_ford_1919.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Henry_ford_1919.jpg/170px-Henry_ford_1919.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="2226"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 217px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Henry_ford_1919.jpg/170px-Henry_ford_1919.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="217" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_ford_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> (ca. 1919)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1910Ford-T.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1910Ford-T.jpg/220px-1910Ford-T.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="527"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 173px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1910Ford-T.jpg/220px-1910Ford-T.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="173" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1910Ford-T.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1910 <a href="/wiki/Model_T" class="mw-redirect" title="Model T">Model T</a>, photographed in <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_Company" title="Henry Ford Company">Henry Ford Company</a> was Henry Ford's first attempt at a car manufacturing company and was established on November 3, 1901. This became the <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_Motor_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadillac Motor Company">Cadillac Motor Company</a> on August 22, 1902, after Ford left with the rights to his name.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The Ford Motor Company was launched in a converted factory in 1903 with $28,000 (equivalent to $797,000 in 2019) in cash from twelve investors, most notably <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_Dodge" title="John Francis Dodge">John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horace_Elgin_Dodge" title="Horace Elgin Dodge">Horace Dodge</a> (who would later found <a href="/wiki/Dodge_Brothers_Motor_Vehicle_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Dodge Brothers Motor Vehicle Company">their own</a> car company). The first president was not Ford, but local banker <a href="/wiki/John_S._Gray_(Michigan)" class="mw-redirect" title="John S. Gray (Michigan)">John S. Gray</a>, who was chosen to assuage investors' fears that Ford would leave the new company the way he had left its predecessor.  During its early years, the company produced just a few cars a day at its factory on <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mack_Avenue_Plant" title="Ford Mack Avenue Plant">Mack Avenue</a> and later at its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Piquette_Avenue_Plant" title="Ford Piquette Avenue Plant">factory on Piquette Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>. Groups of two or three men worked on each car, assembling it from parts made mostly by supplier companies contracting for Ford. Within a decade, the company would lead the world in the expansion and refinement of the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> concept, and Ford soon brought much of the part production in-house (<a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertical integration</a>).
</p><p>Henry Ford was 39 years old when he founded the Ford Motor Company, which would go on to become one of the world's largest and most profitable companies. It has been in continuous family control for over 100 years and is one of the largest family-controlled companies in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The first gasoline-powered <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobile</a> had been created in 1885 by the <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> inventor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Benz" title="Karl Benz">Carl Benz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Benz_Patent-Motorwagen" title="Benz Patent-Motorwagen">Benz Patent-Motorwagen</a>). More efficient production methods were needed to make automobiles affordable for the middle class, to which Ford contributed by, for instance, introducing the first moving <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> in 1913 at the Ford <a href="/wiki/Highland_Park_Ford_Plant" title="Highland Park Ford Plant">factory in Highland Park</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Between 1903 and 1908, Ford produced the Models <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_A_(1903-04)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Model A (1903-04)">A</a>, B, C, F, K, N, R, and S. Hundreds or a few thousand of most of these were sold per year. In 1908, Ford introduced the mass-produced <a href="/wiki/Model_T" class="mw-redirect" title="Model T">Model T</a>, which totaled millions sold over nearly 20 years. In 1927, Ford replaced the T with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_A_(1927%E2%80%931931)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Model A (1927–1931)">Model A</a>, the first car with safety glass in the windshield.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Ford launched the <a href="/wiki/Ford_flathead_V8" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford flathead V8">first low-priced car with a V8</a> engine in 1932.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In an attempt to compete with General Motors' mid-priced Pontiac, Oldsmobile, and Buick, Ford created the Mercury in 1939 as a higher-priced companion car to Ford.  Henry Ford purchased the Lincoln Motor Company in 1922, in order to compete with such brands as Cadillac and Packard for the luxury segment of the automobile market.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 1929, Ford was contracted by the government of the Soviet Union to set up the <a href="/wiki/GAZ" title="GAZ">Gorky Automobile Plant</a> in Russia initially producing Ford Model A and AAs thereby playing an important role in the industrialization of that country.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Ford_Germany" title="Ford Germany">Ford Germany</a>, Ford's subsidiary in Germany, produced military vehicles and other equipment for <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>'s <a href="/wiki/German_re-armament" title="German re-armament">war effort</a>. Some of Ford's operations in Germany at the time were run using <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">forced labor</a>.
</p><p>The creation of a scientific laboratory in Dearborn, Michigan in 1951, doing unfettered basic research, led to Ford's unlikely involvement in <a href="/wiki/Superconductivity" title="Superconductivity">superconductivity</a> research. In 1964, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_Research_Labs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford Research Labs (page does not exist)">Ford Research Labs</a> made a key breakthrough with the invention of a superconducting quantum interference device or <a href="/wiki/SQUID" title="SQUID">SQUID</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>Ford offered the Lifeguard safety package from 1956, which included such innovations as a standard deep-dish steering wheel, optional front, and, for the first time in a car, rear seatbelts, and an optional padded dash.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Ford introduced child-proof door locks into its products in 1957, and, in the same year, offered the first retractable hardtop on a mass-produced six-seater car.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In late 1955, Ford established the Continental division as a separate luxury car division.  This division was responsible for the manufacture and sale of the famous Continental Mark II.  At the same time, the Edsel division was created to design and market that car starting with the 1958 model year.  Due to limited sales of the Continental and the Edsel disaster, Ford merged Mercury, Edsel, and Lincoln into "M-E-L," which reverted to "Lincoln-Mercury" after Edsel's November 1959 demise.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The Ford Mustang was introduced on April 17, 1964 during New York World's Fair (where Ford had a pavilion made by <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a>.)<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1965, Ford introduced the seat belt reminder light.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>With the 1980s, Ford introduced several highly successful vehicles around the world. During the 1980s, Ford began using the advertising slogan, "Have you driven a Ford, lately?" to introduce new customers to their brand and make their vehicles appear more modern. In 1990 and 1994 respectively, Ford also acquired <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar Cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>  During the mid- to late 1990s, Ford continued to sell large numbers of vehicles, in a booming <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> economy with a soaring stock market and low fuel prices.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>With the dawn of the new century, legacy <a href="/wiki/Health_care_prices_in_the_United_States" title="Health care prices in the United States">health care costs</a>, higher fuel prices, and a faltering economy led to falling market shares, declining sales, and diminished profit margins. Most of the corporate profits came from financing consumer automobile loans through <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Credit_Company" title="Ford Motor Credit Company">Ford Motor Credit Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bill_Ford_2011.jpg/170px-Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2492" data-file-height="3502"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 239px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bill_Ford_2011.jpg/170px-Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="239" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Clay_Ford_Jr." title="William Clay Ford Jr.">William Clay Ford Jr.</a>, great-grandson of Henry Ford, serves as the <a href="/wiki/Executive_chairman" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive chairman">executive chairman</a> at the board of Ford Motor Company</div></div></div>
<p>By 2005, both Ford and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">GM</a>'s corporate bonds had been downgraded to junk status<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> as a result of high U.S. health care costs for an <a href="/wiki/Aging_in_the_American_workforce" title="Aging in the American workforce">aging workforce</a>, soaring gasoline prices, eroding market share, and an overdependence on declining <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> sales. Profit margins decreased on large vehicles due to increased "incentives" (in the form of rebates or low-interest financing) to offset declining demand.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In the latter half of 2005, Chairman Bill Ford asked newly-appointed Ford Americas Division President <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a> to develop a plan to return the company to profitability. Fields previewed the Plan, named <i><a href="/wiki/The_Way_Forward" title="The Way Forward">The Way Forward</a></i>, at the December 7, 2005, board meeting of the company and it was unveiled to the public on January 23, 2006. "The Way Forward" included resizing the company to match market realities, dropping some unprofitable and inefficient models, consolidating production lines, closing 14 factories and cutting 30,000 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>Ford moved to introduce a range of new vehicles, including "<a href="/wiki/Crossover_SUV" class="mw-redirect" title="Crossover SUV">Crossover SUVs</a>" built on <a href="/wiki/Unibody" class="mw-redirect" title="Unibody">unibody</a> car platforms, rather than more <a href="/wiki/Body-on-frame" title="Body-on-frame">body-on-frame</a> chassis. In developing the hybrid electric powertrain technologies for the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escape Hybrid">Ford Escape Hybrid</a> SUV, Ford licensed similar Toyota hybrid technologies<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> to avoid patent infringements.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Ford announced that it will team up with electricity supply company <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Edison" title="Southern California Edison">Southern California Edison</a> (SCE) to examine the future of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> in terms of how home and vehicle energy systems will work with the electrical grid. Under the multimillion-dollar, multi-year project, Ford will convert a demonstration fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escape Hybrid">Ford Escape Hybrids</a> into plug-in hybrids, and SCE will evaluate how the vehicles might interact with the home and the utility's electrical grid. Some of the vehicles will be evaluated "in typical customer settings", according to Ford.<sup id="cite_ref-akhrum_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhrum-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-edison_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edison-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Clay_Ford_Jr." title="William Clay Ford Jr.">William Clay Ford Jr.</a>, great-grandson of Henry Ford (and better known by his nickname "Bill"), was appointed executive chairman in 1998, and also became chief executive officer of the company in 2001, with the departure of <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Nasser" title="Jacques Nasser">Jacques Nasser</a>, becoming the first member of the Ford family to head the company since the retirement of his uncle, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_II" title="Henry Ford II">Henry Ford II</a>, in 1982. Ford sold motorsport engineering company <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Forsythe" title="Gerald Forsythe">Gerald Forsythe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Kalkhoven" title="Kevin Kalkhoven">Kevin Kalkhoven</a> in 2004, the start of a decrease in Ford's motorsport involvement. Upon the retirement of president and chief operations officer Jim Padilla in April 2006, Bill Ford assumed his roles as well. Five months later, in September, Ford named <a href="/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> as president and CEO, with Ford continuing as executive chairman. In December 2006, the company raised its borrowing capacity to about $25 billion, placing substantially all corporate assets as collateral.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Chairman Bill Ford has stated that "bankruptcy is not an option".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Ford and the <a href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">United Auto Workers</a>, representing approximately 46,000 hourly workers in North America, agreed to a historic contract settlement in November 2007 giving the company a substantial break in terms of its ongoing retiree health care costs and other economic issues. The agreement included the establishment of a company-funded, independently run <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_Employee_Beneficiary_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association">Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association</a> (VEBA) trust to shift the burden of retiree health care from the company's books, thereby improving its balance sheet. This arrangement took effect on January 1, 2010. As a sign of its currently strong cash position, Ford contributed its entire current liability (estimated at approximately <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$5.5 billion</span> as of December 31, 2009) to the VEBA in cash, and also pre-paid <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500 million</span> of its future liabilities to the fund. The agreement also gives hourly workers the job security they were seeking by having the company commit to substantial investments in most of its factories.
</p><p>The automaker reported the largest annual loss in company history in 2006 of $12.7 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and estimated that it would not return to profitability until 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> However, Ford surprised <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> in the second quarter of 2007 by posting a $750 million profit. Despite the gains, the company finished the year with a $2.7 billion loss, largely attributed to finance restructuring at <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>On June 2, 2008, Ford sold its Jaguar and Land Rover operations to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> for $2.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-r_20080602_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r_20080602-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>During congressional hearings held in November 2008 at Washington D.C., and in a show of support, Ford's Alan Mulally stated that "We at Ford are hopeful that we have enough liquidity. But we also must prepare ourselves for the prospect of further deteriorating economic conditions". Mulally went on to state that "The collapse of one of our competitors would have a severe impact on Ford" and that Ford Motor Company supports both Chrysler and General Motors in their search for government bridge loans in the face of conditions caused by the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932012_global_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2012 global financial crisis">2008 financial crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Together, the three companies presented action plans for the sustainability of the industry. Mulally stated that "In addition to our plan, we are also here today to request support for the industry. In the near-term, Ford does not require access to a government bridge loan. However, we request a credit line of $9 billion as a critical backstop or safeguard against worsening conditions as we drive transformational change in our company"<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> GM and Chrysler received government loans and financing through <a href="/wiki/T.A.R.P." class="mw-redirect" title="T.A.R.P.">T.A.R.P.</a> legislation funding provisions.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>On December 19, the cost of <a href="/wiki/Credit_default_swap" title="Credit default swap">credit default swaps</a> to insure the debt of Ford was 68 percent the sum insured for five years in addition to annual payments of 5 percent. That meant $6.8 million paid upfront to insure $10 million in debt, in addition to payments of $500,000 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In January 2009, Ford reported a $14.6 billion loss in the preceding year, a record for the company. The company retained sufficient liquidity to fund its operations. Through April 2009, Ford's strategy of debt for equity exchanges erased $9.9 billion in liabilities (28% of its total) in order to leverage its cash position.<sup id="cite_ref-Dolan_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dolan-41">[41]</a></sup> These actions yielded Ford a $2.7 billion profit in fiscal year 2009, the company's first full-year profit in four years.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2012, Ford's corporate bonds were upgraded from junk to investment grade again, citing sustainable, lasting improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p><p>On October 29, 2012, Ford announced the sale of its climate control components business, its last remaining automotive components operation, to Detroit Thermal Systems LLC for an undisclosed price.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>On November 1, 2012, Ford announced that <a href="/wiki/CEO" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> will stay with the company until 2014. Ford also named <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a>, the president of operations in Americas, as its new chief operating officer<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Ford's CEO Mulally was paid a compensation of over $174 million in his previous seven years at Ford since 2006. The generous amount has been a sore point for some workers of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2016, Ford announced a plan to modernize its Dearborn engineering and headquarters campuses through a ten-year building project. The end result would see the number of Ford employees working in these areas doubling, to 24,000. During construction, some 2000 of the employees were relocated out of the campus to a temporary location in a disused section of the local shopping mall.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Facilities would also be altered to allow ride-sharing and electric and self-driving vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Estimates of the construction cost were $1.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michigan_Central_Train_Station_Exterior_2010.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Michigan_Central_Train_Station_Exterior_2010.jpg/220px-Michigan_Central_Train_Station_Exterior_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4295" data-file-height="2864"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Michigan_Central_Train_Station_Exterior_2010.jpg/220px-Michigan_Central_Train_Station_Exterior_2010.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michigan_Central_Train_Station_Exterior_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The historic, once abandoned <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Central_Station" title="Michigan Central Station">Michigan Central Station</a> was purchased by Ford Motor Company in May 2018 and is expected to undergo a significant four-year renovation</div></div></div> 
<p>On January 3, 2017, Ford <a href="/wiki/CEO" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a> announced that in a "vote of confidence" because of the pro-business climate being fostered in part by <a href="/wiki/President-elect_of_the_United_States" title="President-elect of the United States">President-elect</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, Ford has canceled plans to invest $1.6 billion in a new plant in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> to manufacture the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Ford Focus</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Ford Focus</a> will now be manufactured in the existing plant in Mexico. Instead, Fields announced that Ford will be investing $700 million in <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, which it plans to use to create 700 new jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Also in 2017, Ford began development of a new mixed-use urban campus in <a href="/wiki/Corktown,_Detroit" title="Corktown, Detroit">the Corktown neighborhood of Detroit</a>, with its purchase, renovation, and occupation of The Factory at Michigan and Rosa Parks. The new site was expected to have a major focus on the development of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous vehicle">autonomous vehicle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicle</a> technology.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Ford later began buying up other parcels of land in Corktown including a very high-profile purchase of <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Central_Station" title="Michigan Central Station">Michigan Central Station</a> which is planned to become the hub of their Corktown campus, and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Warehouse" title="Roosevelt Warehouse">Roosevelt Warehouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Ford expects to move 2,500 of its employees, roughly 5 percent of its southeast Michigan workforce, to the campus with space for an additional 2,500 entrepreneurs, technology companies and partners.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Bill Ford envisioned the first-floor concourse of the train station to be a public gathering place with retail outlets and restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2017, Ford Motor Co. acquired majority ownership of Argo AI, a self-driving car startup.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2017, Ford announced cuts to its global workforce amid efforts to address the company's declining share price and to improve profits. The company is targeting $3 billion in cost reduction and a nearly 10% reduction in the salaried workforce in Asia and North America to enhance earnings in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Jim Hackett was announced to replace Mark Fields as CEO of Ford Motor. Mr. Hackett most recently oversaw the formation of Ford Smart Mobility, a unit responsible for experimenting with car-sharing programs, self-driving ventures and other programs aimed at helping Ford better compete with <a href="/wiki/Uber" title="Uber">Uber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a> and other tech giants looking to edge in on the auto industry.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>On April 25, 2018, Ford announced that it will discontinue passenger cars in the North American market in the next four years, except for the Mustang, due to declining demand and profitability.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The Focus Active, a crossover SUV based on the newly-unveiled fourth-generation Focus, was also intended to be marketed in the United States. Due to the vehicle being manufactured in China, Ford later announced that it would not release the Focus Active in the United States, due to <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_trade_war" title="China–United States trade war">tariffs imposed by the Trump administration on Chinese exports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2020, the Detroit <a href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">United Auto Workers</a> union announced that after discussion with the leaders of <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, Ford, and <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler_Automobiles" title="Fiat Chrysler Automobiles">Fiat Chrysler Automobiles</a>, the carmakers would partially shut down factories on a "rotating" basis to combat the <a href="/wiki/2019-20_coronavirus_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="2019-20 coronavirus pandemic">coronavirus pandemic outbreak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On March 24, representatives of Ford announced that production in the US, Canada, and Mexico will not resume on March 30 as it was originally planned amid the further coronavirus pandemic spread.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
