<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_management">Executive management</span></h3>
<p>Members of the Ford board as of October 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> are: Stephen Butler, <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Casiano" title="Kimberly Casiano">Kimberly Casiano</a>, Anthony F. Earley, Jr., <a href="/wiki/Edsel_Ford_II" title="Edsel Ford II">Edsel Ford II</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Clay_Ford_Jr." title="William Clay Ford Jr.">William Clay Ford Jr.</a> (executive chairman), <a href="/wiki/James_Hackett_(businessman)" title="James Hackett (businessman)">Jim Hackett</a> (president and CEO), William W. Helman IV, <a href="/wiki/William_E._Kennard" class="mw-redirect" title="William E. Kennard">William E. Kennard</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_C._Lechleiter" title="John C. Lechleiter">John C. Lechleiter</a>, Ellen Marram, <a href="/wiki/John_L._Thornton" title="John L. Thornton">John L. Thornton</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Veihmeyer" class="mw-redirect" title="John Veihmeyer">John Veihmeyer</a>, Lynn Vojvodich, and John S. Weinberg.<sup id="cite_ref-fmci_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fmci-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_Motor_Company_Fund">Ford Motor Company Fund</span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>The Ford Motor Company Fund (also known as Ford Fund, not affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">Ford Foundation</a>), based in Dearborn, Michigan, is the philanthropic arm of the Ford Motor Company.<sup id="cite_ref-fordfund2016_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fordfund2016-66">[66]</a></sup> Established in 1949<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_II" title="Henry Ford II">Henry Ford II</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, Ford Fund is a nonprofit corporate foundation<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> financed by contributions from Ford Motor Company. In 2017, Ford Fund contributed $63 million<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> to various causes<sup id="cite_ref-fordfund2016_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fordfund2016-66">[66]</a></sup> with a focus on education, driving safely and community building.
</p><p>The Ford Driving Skills for Life program is a driver safety program aimed at teens that were developed together with the Governors Highway Safety Association and safety experts.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The Ford Volunteer Corps allows Ford employees and retirees to sign up for volunteering work on local projects in more than 40 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The Ford Fund invests $18 million annually in education in the United States and around the world, but accepts applications only from nonprofit organizations registered in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Education programs and scholarships include Alan Mulally Engineering Scholarship, Ford Blue Oval Scholars Program, Ford College Community Challenge (Ford C3), Ford Driving Dreams Tour, Ford Fund/Detroit Free Press Journalism Scholarship, Ford Next Generation Learning (Ford NGL), Grants to Individuals Program, HBCU Community Challenge, Smithsonian Latino Center Young Ambassadors Program, and William Clay Ford Automotive Design Scholarship.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>Ford has had manufacturing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_factories" title="List of Ford factories">operations</a> worldwide, including in the United States, Canada, Mexico, China, India, the United Kingdom, Germany, Turkey, Brazil, Argentina, Australia, and South Africa. Ford also has a cooperative agreement with Russian automaker <a href="/wiki/GAZ" title="GAZ">GAZ</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike,_Mineola,_Garden_City.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg/220px-The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1453" data-file-height="909"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 138px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg/220px-The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="138" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike,_Mineola,_Garden_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ford dealer in <a href="/wiki/Garden_City,_New_York" title="Garden City, New York">Garden City, New York</a>, ca. 1930–1945</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2010, Ford reported that its sales increased 23% for the month, and that 37% of its sales came from fleet sales.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In June 2010, Sales to individual customers at dealerships increased 13% while fleet sales rose by 32%.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In the first seven months of 2010, fleet sales of Ford for the same period rose 35% to 386,000 units while retail sales increase 19%.<sup id="cite_ref-AutomotiveNews_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutomotiveNews-75">[75]</a></sup> Fleet sales account for 39 percent of Chrysler's sales and 31 percent for GM's.<sup id="cite_ref-AutomotiveNews_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutomotiveNews-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Europe" title="Ford of Europe">Ford of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg/220px-Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg/220px-Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ford's <a href="/wiki/Dunton_Technical_Centre" title="Dunton Technical Centre">Dunton Technical Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Laindon" title="Laindon">Laindon</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the largest automotive research and development facility in the country<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/220px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1176"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 126px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/220px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="126" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ford Research Center in <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a></div></div></div>
<p>At first, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Germany" title="Ford Germany">Ford in Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Britain" title="Ford of Britain">Ford in Britain</a> built different models from one another until 1965, when the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Ford Transit</a> and later the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Ford Escort</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Capri" title="Ford Capri">Ford Capri</a> became common to both companies. In 1970, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taunus" title="Ford Taunus">Ford Taunus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Ford Cortina</a> came into production with a common base construction, both models being produced in <a href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Left hand drive">left hand drive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right_hand_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Right hand drive">right hand drive</a>. Later on, the models became identical and the respective models right and left hand drive exclusively.  Rationalisation of model ranges meant that production of many models in the UK switched to elsewhere in Europe, including Belgium and Spain as well as Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a> replaced the Taunus and Cortina in 1982, drawing criticism for its radical aerodynamic styling, which was soon given nicknames, the "Jellymould" and "The Salesman's Spaceship."
</p><p>In February 2002, Ford ended car production in the UK. It was the first time in 90 years that Ford cars had not been made in Britain, although production of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Transit</a> van continued at the company's <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> facility until mid-2013, engines at <a href="/wiki/Bridgend" title="Bridgend">Bridgend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Dagenham" title="Ford Dagenham">Dagenham</a>, and transmissions at <a href="/wiki/Halewood" title="Halewood">Halewood</a>. Development of European Ford is broadly split between <a href="/wiki/Dunton_Wayletts" title="Dunton Wayletts">Dunton</a> in Essex (powertrain, Fiesta/Ka, and commercial vehicles) and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> (body, chassis, electrical, Focus, Mondeo) in Germany. Ford also produced the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Trader" title="Thames Trader">Thames</a> range of commercial vehicles, although the use of this brand name was discontinued circa 1965. Elsewhere in continental Europe, Ford assembles the Mondeo, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Galaxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_S-Max" title="Ford S-Max">S-Max</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Kuga" title="Ford Kuga">Kuga</a><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> in Valencia (Spain), Fiesta in Cologne (Germany), Focus in <a href="/wiki/Saarlouis" title="Saarlouis">Saarlouis</a> (Germany), Ecosport<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Puma_(sport_compact)" title="Ford Puma (sport compact)">Puma</a><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Craiova" title="Craiova">Craiova</a> (Romania).
</p><p>Ford also owns a joint-venture production plant in Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Otosan" class="mw-redirect" title="Otosan">Ford Otosan</a>, established in the 1970s, manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Transit Connect</a> compact panel van as well as the "Jumbo" and long-wheelbase versions of the full-size Transit. This new production facility was set up near <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a> in 2002, and its opening marked the end of Transit assembly in Genk.
</p><p>Another joint venture plant near <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Setúbal">Setúbal</a> in Portugal, set up in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, formerly assembled the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Galaxy</a> people-carrier as well as its sister ships, the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Sharan" title="Volkswagen Sharan">VW Sharan</a> and <a href="/wiki/SEAT_Alhambra" title="SEAT Alhambra">SEAT Alhambra</a>. With the introduction of the third generation of the Galaxy, Ford has moved the production of the people-carrier to the Genk plant, with Volkswagen taking over sole ownership of the Setúbal facility.
</p><p>In 2008, Ford acquired a majority stake in <a href="/wiki/Automobile_Craiova" title="Automobile Craiova">Automobile Craiova</a>, Romania. Starting 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Ford Transit Connect</a> was Ford's first model produced in <a href="/wiki/Craiova" title="Craiova">Craiova</a>, followed, in 2012, by low-capacity car engines and a new small class car, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_B-Max" title="Ford B-Max">B-Max</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p><p>Its 1959 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Anglia" title="Ford Anglia">Anglia</a> two-door saloon was one of the most quirky-looking small family cars in Europe at the time of its launch, but buyers soon became accustomed to its looks and it was hugely popular with British buyers in particular. It was still selling well when replaced by the more practical <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Escort</a> in 1967.
</p><p>The third incarnation of the Ford Escort was launched in 1980 and marked the company's move from rear-wheel drive saloons to front-wheel drive hatchbacks in the small family car sector.
</p><p>The fourth generation Escort was produced from 1990 until 2000, although its successor – the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus (international)">Focus</a> – had been on sale since 1998. On its launch, the Focus was arguably the most dramatic-looking and fine-handling small family cars on sale and sold in huge volumes right up to the launch of the next generation Focus at the end of 2004.
</p><p>The 1982 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a> – replacement for the long-running and massively popular <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Cortina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taunus" title="Ford Taunus">Taunus</a> models – was a style-setter at the time of its launch. Its ultramodern aerodynamic design was a world away from a boxy, sharp-edged Cortina, and it was massively popular just about everywhere it was sold. A series of updates kept it looking relatively fresh until it was replaced by the front-wheel drive <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> at the start of 1993.
</p><p>The rise in popularity of small cars during the 1970s saw Ford enter the mini-car market in 1976 with its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a> hatchback. Most of its production was concentrated at <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencia, Spain">Valencia</a> in Spain, and the Fiesta sold in huge figures from the very start. An update in 1983 and the launch of an all-new model in 1989 strengthened its position in the small car market.
</p><p>On October 24, 2012, Ford announced that it would be closing its <a href="/wiki/Genk" title="Genk">Genk</a> assembly plant in eastern <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> by the end of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, Ford announced that it took control of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sollers" title="Ford Sollers">Ford Sollers</a>, Ford's joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> company <a href="/wiki/Sollers_JSC" title="Sollers JSC">Sollers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2018, at the IAA Commercial Vehicles show in Hannover, Germany, Ford introduced an electric tractor trailer concept vehicle dubbed the F-Vision, which would have Level 4 autonomous driving capability.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="East_and_Southeast_Asia">East and Southeast Asia</span></h3>
<p>Ford formed its first passenger-vehicle joint venture in China in 2001, six years behind GM and more than a decade after VW. It has spent as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> $4.9 billion to expand its lineup and double production capacity in China to 600,000 vehicles. This includes Ford's largest-ever factory complex in the southwestern city of Chongqing. Ford had 2.5% of the Chinese market in 2013, while VW controlled 14.5% and GM had 15.6%, according to consultant LMC Automotive. GM outsells Ford in China by more than six-to-one.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Ford's presence in Asia has traditionally been much smaller, confined to <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Singapore, Hong Kong, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, where Ford has had a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Ford_Lio_Ho_Motor" title="Ford Lio Ho Motor">Lio Ho</a> since the 1970s. Ford began assembly of cars in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> in 1960, but withdrew from the country in 1976, and did not return until 1995 when it formed a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> called Auto Alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Now based in the Bo-win Sub District of the Sriracha District in <a href="/wiki/Chonburi_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chonburi (city)">Chonburi</a>, the factory still produces passenger automobiles. The factory built in 1941 in Singapore was shortly taken over by the Japanese during the war and was the site of a surrender of the British to the Japanese, at the <a href="/wiki/Old_Ford_Motor_Factory" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Ford Motor Factory">factory site</a> which is now a national monument in Singapore.
On April 30, 2013, Ford Motor Co. launched their car and truck line in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>. Previously, heavy importation taxes had stifled imported car purchases in Myanmar, but due to currency reform, lifting of previous import restrictions, and the abolishment of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_controls" title="Foreign exchange controls">shadow currency</a>, Myanmar's car market had grown in demand.<sup id="cite_ref-investvine_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investvine-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_of_Korea">Ford of Korea</span></h4>
<p>In 1967, Ford partnered with the South Korean company <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a>, and at the new factory in <a href="/wiki/Ulsan,_South_Korea" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulsan, South Korea">Ulsan, South Korea</a>, built the European <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Ford Cortina</a> until 1974 when Hyundai introduced their all-new <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Pony" title="Hyundai Pony">Hyundai Pony</a> in 1975. Ford then developed a relationship with Korea's oldest car manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia</a> which built vehicles co-engineered with <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>, later selling the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Ford Festiva</a> from 1988–1993, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Ford Aspire</a> from 1994–1997 for export to the United States. With the acquisition of a stake in Japanese manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> in 1979, Ford began selling Mazda's <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Familia" title="Mazda Familia">Familia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Capella" title="Mazda Capella">Capella</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Laser" title="Ford Laser">Ford Laser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a> throughout the region, replacing the European-sourced Escort and Cortina. Ford lost their Kia interest to Hyundai in 1998 during the <a href="/wiki/Asian_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian financial crisis">Asian financial crisis</a>. Kia had declared bankruptcy in 1997; in 1998, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai Motor Company</a> acquired 51% of the company, outbidding Ford which had owned an interest in Kia Motors since 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> After subsequent divestments,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Hyundai Motor Company owns less than 50% of the company but remains Kia's largest stakeholder.
</p><p>Ford currently sells the Focus and Mondeo with diesel engines, plus the Mustang, Taurus, Escape, and Explorer, as well as the Lincoln MKS, MKZ, and MKC.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="South_and_West_Asia">South and West Asia</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ford_India_Private_Limited" title="Ford India Private Limited">Ford India</a> began production in 1998 at <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a>, with its Ford Escort model, which was later replaced by the locally produced <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ikon" title="Ford Ikon">Ford Ikon</a> in 2001. It has since added the Fusion, Fiesta, Mondeo and Endeavour models to its product line.
</p><p>On March 9, 2010, Ford launched its first made-for-India compact car. Starting at <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">₹</a>349,900, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Figo" title="Ford Figo">Figo</a> was Ford's first car designed and priced for the mass Indian market.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> On July 28, 2011, Ford India signed a memorandum of understanding (MoU) with the State of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> for the construction of an assembly and engine plant in <a href="/wiki/Sanand" title="Sanand">Sanand</a> and planned to invest approximately <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 billion</span> on a 460-acre site.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In 2019, the company and <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_%26_Mahindra" title="Mahindra &amp; Mahindra">Mahindra &amp; Mahindra</a> formed a joint venture to develop, market and distribute Ford-branded vehicles in India.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>Ford's market presence in the Middle East has traditionally been small, partly due to previous Arab boycotts of companies dealing with Israel. Ford and Lincoln vehicles are currently marketed in ten countries in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia, Kuwait, and the United Arab Emirates are the biggest markets. Ford also established itself in Egypt in 1926 but faced an uphill battle during the 1950s due to the hostile nationalist business environment.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Ford's distributor in Saudi Arabia announced in February 2003 that it had sold 100,000 Ford and Lincoln vehicles since commencing sales in November 1986. Half of the Ford and Lincoln vehicles sold in that country were <a href="/wiki/Ford_Crown_Victoria" title="Ford Crown Victoria">Ford Crown Victorias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2004, Ford sold 30,000 units in the region, falling far short of General Motors' 88,852 units and <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan Motors</a>' 75,000 units.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span></h3>
<p>In South America, Ford's primary operations are in <a href="/wiki/Ford_Brasil" title="Ford Brasil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Argentina" title="Ford Motor Argentina">Argentina</a>, and Ford Andina<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> (Colombia, Ecuador, and Venezuela). Ford employs over 18,000 people and operates seven assembly or other plants in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In 1987, Ford Brasil and Ford Motor Argentina merged their operations with the Brazilian and Argentine operations of <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>, forming a new joint-venture company called <a href="/wiki/Autolatina" class="mw-redirect" title="Autolatina">Autolatina</a> with a shared model range.<sup id="cite_ref-FolhadeS.Paulo_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FolhadeS.Paulo-100">[100]</a></sup> Autolatina was dissolved in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-FolhadeS.Paulo_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FolhadeS.Paulo-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span></h3>
<p>In Africa, Ford's market presence has traditionally been strongest in South Africa and neighbouring countries, with only trucks being sold elsewhere on the continent. Ford in South Africa began by importing kits from Canada to be assembled at its Port Elizabeth facility. Later Ford sourced its models from the UK and Australia, with local versions of the Ford Cortina including the XR6, with a 3.0 V6 engine, and a <a href="/wiki/Ford_P100" title="Ford P100">Cortina-based 'bakkie' or pick-up</a>, which was exported to the UK. In the mid-1980s, Ford merged with a rival company, owned by <a href="/wiki/Anglo_American_plc" title="Anglo American plc">Anglo American</a>, to form the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Motor_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="South African Motor Corporation">South African Motor Corporation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Samcor" title="Samcor">Samcor</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>Following international condemnation of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, Ford divested from South Africa in 1988, and sold its stake in Samcor, although it licensed the use of its brand name to the company.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Samcor began to assemble Mazdas as well, which affected its product line-up and saw the European Fords like the Escort and Sierra replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>-based Laser<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Ford bought a 45 per cent stake in <a href="/wiki/Samcor" title="Samcor">Samcor</a> following the demise of apartheid in 1994, and this later became, once again, a wholly owned subsidiary, the Ford Motor Company of Southern Africa. Ford now sells a local sedan version of the Fiesta (also built in India and Mexico), and the Focus. The Falcon model from Australia was also sold in South Africa but was dropped in 2003 while the Mondeo, after briefly being assembled locally, was dropped in 2005. The Mondeo was later reintroduced in 2015, badged as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_(Americas)" title="Ford Fusion (Americas)">Fusion</a> but was dropped in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h3>
<p>Ford Research and Innovation Center is the name of the technology research facilities of Ford Motor Company in
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">Dearborn, Michigan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto, California</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>, Germany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, China</li></ul><p>The Ford Research and Innovation Center in Palo Alto was first opened in 2012, and in January 2015, announced plans to significantly expand its operations.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_operations">Former operations</span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="East_and_Southeast_Asia_2">East and Southeast Asia</span></h3>
<p>Ford decided to shut down their entire operations in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, including their dealer network by second half of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_of_Japan">Ford of Japan</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Japan" title="Ford Motor Company of Japan">Ford Motor Company of Japan</a></div>
<p>Ford established a manufacturing facility in the port city of Yokohama in February 1925, where Model T vehicles were assembled using imported <a href="/wiki/Knock-down_kit" title="Knock-down kit">knock-down kits</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The factory subsequently produced 10,000 Model A's up to 1936. Production ceased in 1940 as a result of political tensions between Japan and the United States.
</p><p>After World War II, Ford did not have a presence in Japan, as the Ford facility was appropriated by the Japanese Government until 1958 when property was returned as a possession of the Ford Motor Company and became a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mazda_facilities#R&amp;D" title="List of Mazda facilities">research and development location</a> for Ford partner <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>. In 1979, Ford acquired a 24.5% ownership stake in Mazda, and in 1982, Ford and Mazda jointly established a sales channel to sell Ford products in Japan, including vehicles manufactured in North America, at a dealership called <i><a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E3%82%AA%E3%83%BC%E3%83%88%E3%83%A9%E3%83%9E" class="extiw" title="ja:オートラマ">Autorama</a> (Japanese)</i>. The Autorama sales channel was renamed Ford Sales of Japan in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>Vehicles sold at <i>Autorama</i> locations were the North American assembled Ford Explorer, Probe (1989–1998), Mustang, Taurus (1989–1997), Thunderbird (1990–1993), Lincoln Continental, and Lincoln LS. Ford products manufactured in Europe that were sold in Japan were the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ka" title="Ford Ka">Ka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Focus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max" title="Ford C-Max">Focus C-MAX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Galaxy</a>. Mazda manufactured Ford vehicles in Japan and sold them as Fords at the Autorama locations. They were the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Ford Telstar</a> (Mazda Capella), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Laser" title="Ford Laser">Laser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Festiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Demio" title="Mazda Demio">Festiva Mini Wagon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ixion" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Ixion">Ixion</a> (Mazda Premacy), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Freda" title="Ford Freda">Freda</a> (Mazda Bongo Friendee), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Spectron" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Spectron">Spectron</a> (Mazda Bongo), and commercial trucks J80 and the J100 (Mazda Bongo truck).
</p><p>Ford increased its shareholding in Mazda to 33.4% in 1996, but as of July 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is listed at 11%.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Ford did sell a small range of vehicles in Japan; as of October 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Ford Mustang, Escape, Explorer (and Explorer truck), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Kuga" title="Ford Kuga">Ford Kuga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Navigator" title="Lincoln Navigator">Lincoln Navigator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKX" title="Lincoln MKX">Lincoln MKX</a>, and more recently, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ecosport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Ecosport">Ford Ecosport</a> were available in Japan. As of February 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Ford no longer maintains a regional office in Minato, Tokyo, Japan, and sales of new cars in Japan have ended.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Ford_Falcon_(FG_X)_XR6_Turbo_sedan_(23382738252).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg/220px-2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4080" data-file-height="2582"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 139px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg/220px-2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="139" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Ford_Falcon_(FG_X)_XR6_Turbo_sedan_(23382738252).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ford FG X Falcon (Australia) (2014–2016; 2014 model shown)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg/220px-Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="648"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 143px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg/220px-Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="143" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ford stamping plant in <a href="/wiki/Geelong" title="Geelong">Geelong</a>, Victoria, Australia. It closed in 2016.</div></div></div>
<p>In Australia and New Zealand, the popular <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Ford Falcon</a> (1960–2016) had long been considered the average family car and is considerably larger than the Mondeo, Ford's largest car sold in Europe. Between 1960 and 1972, the Falcon was based on a U.S. model of the same name, but since then has been entirely designed and manufactured in Australia until 2016, occasionally being manufactured in New Zealand. Like its <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> rival, the <a href="/wiki/Holden_Commodore" title="Holden Commodore">Holden Commodore</a>, the Falcon used a rear wheel drive layout. High-performance variants of the Falcon running locally built engines produce up to 362 hp (270 kW). A <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9_utility" title="Coupé utility">ute</a> (short for "utility", known in the US as <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickup truck</a>) version is also available with the same range of drivetrains. In addition, Ford Australia sells highly tuned limited-production Falcon sedans and <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">utes</a> through its performance car division, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance_Vehicles" title="Ford Performance Vehicles">Ford Performance Vehicles</a> until it closed in 2014.
</p><p>In Australia, the Commodore and Falcon had traditionally outsold all other cars and comprise over 20% of the new car market. In New Zealand, Ford was second in market share in the first eight months of 2006 with 14.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> More recently, Ford has axed its Falcon-based LWB variant of its lineup– the Fairlane and LTD ranges. Ford discontinued the Fairlane in 2007 and LTD in 2008. Ford had announced that their Geelong engine manufacturing plant would be shut down between 2013 and 2016. They had earlier announced local manufacturing of the Focus small car starting from 2011, but instead decided to import the model from Ford's plant in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p><p>In Australia, the Laser was one of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Motor Company of Australia">Ford Australia</a>'s most successful models and was manufactured in Ford's <a href="/wiki/Homebush,_New_South_Wales" title="Homebush, New South Wales">Homebush</a> plant from 1981 until the plant's closure in September 1994. It outsold the <a href="/wiki/Mazda_323" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazda 323">Mazda 323</a>, despite being almost identical to it because the Laser was manufactured in Australia and Ford was perceived as a local brand.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> According to research carried out by <a href="/wiki/Ford_Australia" title="Ford Australia">Ford Australia</a> in 1984, a third of Laser buyers were unaware that the Ford model was based on the <a href="/wiki/Mazda_323" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazda 323">Mazda 323</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p><p>In New Zealand, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Laser" title="Ford Laser">Ford Laser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a> were assembled alongside the <a href="/wiki/Mazda_323" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazda 323">Mazda 323</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazda_626" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazda 626">626</a> until 1997, at the Vehicle Assemblers of New Zealand (VANZ) plant in <a href="/wiki/Wiri" title="Wiri">Wiri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Sierra</a> wagon was also assembled in New Zealand, owing to the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">station wagons</a> in that market.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>The scheduled closure of Ford's Australian manufacturing base in 2016 was confirmed on May 23, 2013. Headquartered in the Victorian suburb of Broadmeadows, the company had registered losses worth AU$600 million over the five years prior to the announcement. It was noted that the corporate fleet and government sales that account for two-thirds of large, local car sales in Australia are insufficient to keep Ford's products profitable and viable in Australia. The decision will affect 1200 Ford workers—over 600 employees in Geelong and more than 500 in Broadmeadows—who will lose their jobs by October 2016. The closure of Fords plants in Norlane Geelong and Broadmeadows Melbourne occurred on October 7, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobiles">Automobiles</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_vehicles" title="List of Ford vehicles">List of Ford vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lincoln_vehicles" title="List of Lincoln vehicles">List of Lincoln vehicles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mercury_vehicles" title="List of Mercury vehicles">List of Mercury vehicles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Ford_F-150_front_5.19.18.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/2017_Ford_F-150_front_5.19.18.jpg/220px-2017_Ford_F-150_front_5.19.18.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4309" data-file-height="2370"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 121px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/2017_Ford_F-150_front_5.19.18.jpg/220px-2017_Ford_F-150_front_5.19.18.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="121" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Ford_F-150_front_5.19.18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2017 model year <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-Series_(thirteenth_generation)" title="Ford F-Series (thirteenth generation)">F-150</a></div></div></div>
<p>Ford Motor Company sells a broad range of automobiles under the Ford <a href="/wiki/Marque" class="mw-redirect" title="Marque">marque</a> worldwide, and an additional range of luxury automobiles under the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln (automobile)">Lincoln</a> marque in the United States. The company has sold vehicles under a number of other marques during its history. The <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> brand was introduced by Ford in 1939, continuing in production until 2011 when poor sales led to its discontinuation.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In 1958, Ford introduced the <a href="/wiki/Edsel" title="Edsel">Edsel</a> brand, but poor sales led to its discontinuation in 1960. In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Merkur" title="Merkur">Merkur</a> brand was introduced in the United States to market products produced by Ford of Europe; it was discontinued in 1989.
</p><p>Ford acquired the British sports car maker <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> in 1989, later selling it on March 12, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> although retaining an 8% stake.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Ford purchased <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a> of Sweden in 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> selling it to <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_Geely_Holding_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhejiang Geely Holding Group">Zhejiang Geely Holding Group</a> in 2010. In November 2008, it reduced its 33.4% <a href="/wiki/Controlling_interest" title="Controlling interest">controlling interest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> of Japan to a 13.4% non-controlling interest.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p><p>On November 18, 2010, Ford reduced their stake further to just 3%, citing the reduction of ownership would allow greater flexibility to pursue growth in emerging markets. Ford and Mazda remain strategic partners through exchanges of technological information and joint ventures, including an American joint venture plant in Flat Rock, Michigan called <a href="/wiki/Auto_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Auto Alliance">Auto Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Ford sold the United Kingdom-based <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> companies and brands to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> of India in March 2008. In 2015, Ford sold its remaining 3% stake in Mazda.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p><p>On April 25, 2018, Ford announced that it planned to phase out all but one of its North American automobile models (the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Mustang</a> will be the sole surviving model) to focus primarily on trucks and SUVs. Ford had also planned to introduce an "Active" crossover version of the next-generation <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Focus</a>, but canceled those plans due to tariff issues between the United States and China.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
