<td>2002–2014</td>
<td>Australia
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Trucks">Trucks</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_1939.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Ford_1939.jpg/220px-Ford_1939.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="460"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 145px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Ford_1939.jpg/220px-Ford_1939.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="145" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_1939.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An advertisement for the 1939 Ford V-8 pick-up truck</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_truck_1961_ad.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Ford_truck_1961_ad.jpg/170px-Ford_truck_1961_ad.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="619" data-file-height="781"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 214px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Ford_truck_1961_ad.jpg/170px-Ford_truck_1961_ad.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="214" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_truck_1961_ad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An advertisement for the 1961 Ford H-Series truck</div></div></div>
<p>Ford has produced trucks since 1908, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_TT" title="Ford Model TT">Ford Model TT</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_AA" title="Ford Model AA">Model AA</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/1932_Ford#Model_BB_trucks" title="1932 Ford">Model BB</a>. Countries where Ford commercial vehicles are or were formerly produced include Argentina, Australia, Brazil, Canada (also badged as <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a>), France, Germany, India, Netherlands, Philippines, Spain (badged <a href="/wiki/Ebro_trucks" title="Ebro trucks">Ebro</a> too), Turkey, UK (badged also <a href="/wiki/Fordson" title="Fordson">Fordson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thames_Trader" title="Thames Trader">Thames</a>), and the United States.
</p><p>From the 1940s to late 1970s, Ford's <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-Series" title="Ford F-Series">Ford F-Series</a> were used as the base for light trucks for the North American market.
</p><p>Most of these ventures are now extinct. The European one that lasted longest was the lorries arm of <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Britain" title="Ford of Britain">Ford of Britain</a>, which became part of the <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a> group in 1986. Ford had a minority share in the new company and Iveco took over sales and production of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cargo" title="Ford Cargo">Ford Cargo</a> range.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Ford's last significant European truck models were the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transcontinental" title="Ford Transcontinental">Transcontinental</a> and the Cargo.
At the end of 1996, Ford sold the rights to its heavy trucks division to the <a href="/wiki/Freightliner_Trucks" title="Freightliner Trucks">Freightliner Trucks</a> division of Daimler AG, with Ford producing the Cargo, Louisville, and Aeromax, through the 1998 model year.  During the 1998 model year, Freightliner began production of its own versions of Ford-developed trucks in St. Thomas, Ontario, launching the <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Trucks" title="Sterling Trucks">Sterling</a> truck brand.<sup id="cite_ref-sterling_news_release_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sterling_news_release-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>  Slotted between Freightliner and Western Star, Sterling trucks were produced through 2009.
</p><p>Line of heavy trucks made by Ford for the North American market:
</p>
<ul><li>Ford F-Series
<ul><li>"Super Duty/Extra Heavy Duty (1958-1962)</li>
<li>"Big Job" (1951-1957)</li></ul></li>
<li>Ford N-Series (1963-1969)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford L-Series">Ford L-Series trucks</a> (1970-1998)
<ul><li>aka Ford "Louisville Line"</li>
<li>Ford Aeromax (1988-1998)</li>
<li>Ford Louisville (1996-1998)</li>
<li>Sterling (1998-2009)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford C-Series">Ford C-Series</a> (1957-1990)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Cargo" title="Ford Cargo">Ford Cargo/CF-Series</a> (1986-1997)</li>
<li>Ford H-Series (1961-1966)
<ul><li>aka "Two-story Falcon"</li></ul></li>
<li>Ford W-Series (1966-1977)</li>
<li>Ford CL-Series (1978-1995)</li></ul><p>For 1999, Ford briefly withdrew from production of medium-duty trucks.  For the 2001 model year, the company entered into a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Navistar_International" title="Navistar International">Navistar International</a> (the supplier of diesel engines for 1-ton F-Series trucks), named <i>Blue Diamond Truck Company LLC</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BD1_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BD1-136">[136]</a></sup>  As part of the joint venture, sharing a common truck chassis, the two companies would produce medium-duty (Class 6-7) trucks in a Navistar facility in Mexico, with each manufacturer supplying its own powertrain and bodywork, with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-650" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford F-650">Ford F-650/F-750 Super Duty</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_DuraStar" title="International DuraStar">International 4000/DuraStar</a> sharing an assembly line.   In 2006, the joint venture debuted the Ford LCF/International CityStar.<sup id="cite_ref-LCF1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCF1-137">[137]</a></sup>  Using a modified F-Series chassis adopted to fit a Mazda Titan cab, the LCF was a low-cab forward truck that was sold through 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-LCF2_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCF2-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>In Europe, Ford manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Ford Transit</a> jumbo van which is classed as a Large Goods Vehicle and has a payload of up to 2,265 kg, there are options of a panel van, pickup or chassis cab. The Ford Transit is also available as a light van called the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Ford Transit Connect</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger" title="Ford Ranger">Ford Ranger</a> pickup is available.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1980sThomasFordSheffield.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/1980sThomasFordSheffield.jpg/220px-1980sThomasFordSheffield.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/1980sThomasFordSheffield.jpg/220px-1980sThomasFordSheffield.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1980sThomasFordSheffield.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Ford B700 bus chassis, with a body by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Built_Buses" title="Thomas Built Buses">Thomas Built</a></div></div></div>
<p>Ford manufactured complete buses in the company's early history, but today the role of the company has changed to that of a <a href="/wiki/Second_stage_manufacturer" title="Second stage manufacturer">second stage manufacturer</a>. In North America, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_E-Series" title="Ford E-Series">E-Series</a> is still used as a chassis for small school buses and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-650" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford F-650">F-650</a> is used in commercial bus markets. In the 1980s and 1990s, the medium-duty <a href="/wiki/Ford_B-Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford B-Series">B700</a> was a popular chassis used by school bus body manufacturers including <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Built_Buses" title="Thomas Built Buses">Thomas Built</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ward_Body_Works" title="Ward Body Works">Ward</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blue_Bird_Corporation" title="Blue Bird Corporation">Blue Bird</a>, but Ford lost its market share due to industry contraction and agreements between body manufacturers. Older bus models included:
</p><p>Prior to 1936, Ford buses were based on truck bodies:
</p>
<ul><li>Model B – 1930s</li>
<li>Model T – 1920s</li>
<li>F-105 school bus</li></ul><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1937_Ford_Transit_Bus_in_Seattle,_when_new.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1937_Ford_Transit_Bus_in_Seattle%2C_when_new.jpg/220px-1937_Ford_Transit_Bus_in_Seattle%2C_when_new.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1190" data-file-height="910"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 168px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1937_Ford_Transit_Bus_in_Seattle%2C_when_new.jpg/220px-1937_Ford_Transit_Bus_in_Seattle%2C_when_new.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="168" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1937_Ford_Transit_Bus_in_Seattle,_when_new.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1937 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Bus" title="Ford Transit Bus">Ford Transit Bus</a> in Seattle</div></div></div>
<p>In 1936, Ford introduced the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Bus" title="Ford Transit Bus">Ford Transit Bus</a>, a series of small transit buses with bodies built by a second party.  Originally a front-engine design, it was modified to a rear-engine design in 1939.  About 1,000 to 1,200 of the original design were built, and around 12,500 of the rear-engine design, which was in production until 1947<sup id="cite_ref-MCA_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCA-140">[140]</a></sup> (rebranded as the Universal Bus in 1946).
</p><p>Rear-engine Transit Bus chassis model numbers:<sup id="cite_ref-detroittransithistory.info_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detroittransithistory.info-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>09-B/19-B City transit bus – 1939–1941</li>
<li>19-B/29-B City transit bus – 1941–1942</li>
<li>49-B/79-B City transit bus – 1944–1947</li>
<li>69-B City transit bus – 1946–1947</li>
<li>29-B City transit bus – 1946–1947</li>
<li>72-T transit bus – 1944–1945</li></ul><p>After 1946 the Transit City bus was sold as the <i>Universal Bus</i> with the roof changed from fabric/wood to all-metal:
</p>
<ul><li>79-B Universal transit bus – 1946–1947</li></ul><p>Succeeding the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Bus" title="Ford Transit Bus">Ford Transit Bus</a> was the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_8M&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford 8M (page does not exist)">Ford 8M</a> buses:
</p>
<ul><li>8MB transit bus – with Wayne Works 1948–?</li></ul><p>Following World War II and from the 1950s onwards, Ford lost out to <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-detroittransithistory.info_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detroittransithistory.info-141">[141]</a></sup> This led to the end of transit buses for Ford in North America.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ford_B-Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford B-Series">B500 or B-series</a> – 1950–1990s based on Ford F-series truck chassis used by school bus body manufacturers</li></ul><p>In Europe, Ford manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Ford Transit</a> <a href="/wiki/Minibus" title="Minibus">Minibus</a> which is classed in Europe as a Passenger Carrying Vehicle and there are options of 12-, 15-, or 17-seaters.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> In the past, European models included:
</p>
<ul><li>EM</li>
<li>N-138</li>
<li>D series buses (Australia)</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tractors">Tractors</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford-Tractor.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ford-Tractor.jpg/220px-Ford-Tractor.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ford-Tractor.jpg/220px-Ford-Tractor.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford-Tractor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Ford N series tractor</div></div></div>
<p>The "Henry Ford and Son Company" began making <a href="/wiki/Fordson_tractor" class="mw-redirect" title="Fordson tractor">Fordson tractors</a> in Henry's hometown of Springwells (later part of <a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">Dearborn</a>), Michigan from 1907 to 1928, from 1919 to 1932, at <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, Ireland, and 1933–1964 at <a href="/wiki/Ford_Dagenham" title="Ford Dagenham">Dagenham</a>, England, later transferred to <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a>. They were also produced in <a href="/wiki/Leningrad" class="mw-redirect" title="Leningrad">Leningrad</a> beginning in 1924.
</p><p>In 1986, Ford expanded its tractor business when it purchased the Sperry-New Holland skid-steer loader and hay baler, hay tools and implement company from <a href="/wiki/Sperry_Corporation" title="Sperry Corporation">Sperry Corporation</a> and formed Ford-New Holland which bought out <a href="/wiki/Versatile_(company)" title="Versatile (company)">Versatile</a> tractors in 1988. This company was bought by <a href="/wiki/Fiat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> in 1993 and the name changed from Ford New Holland to New Holland. <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_Ag" class="mw-redirect" title="New Holland Ag">New Holland</a> is now part of <a href="/wiki/CNH_Global" class="mw-redirect" title="CNH Global">CNH Global</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span></h3>
<p>Ford offers automotive finance through <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Credit_Company" title="Ford Motor Credit Company">Ford Motor Credit Company</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Automotive_components">Automotive components</span></h3>
<p>Ford's <i>FoMoCo</i> parts division sells aftermarket parts under the <a href="/wiki/Motorcraft" title="Motorcraft">Motorcraft</a> brand name. It has spun off its parts division under the name <a href="/wiki/Visteon" title="Visteon">Visteon</a>.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">Motorsport</span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance" title="Ford Performance">Ford Performance</a></div>
<p>Along with <a href="/wiki/Carroll_Shelby_International" title="Carroll Shelby International">Shelby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a>, Ford is one of only three American constructors to win titles on the international scene at the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile">FIA</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_world_championships#Open" class="mw-redirect" title="List of world championships">World Championships</a>. As a constructor, Ford won the <a href="/wiki/World_Sportscar_Championship" title="World Sportscar Championship">World Sportscar Championship</a> three times in <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Sportscar_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1966 World Sportscar Championship season">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967_World_Sportscar_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1967 World Sportscar Championship season">1967</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1968_World_Sportscar_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1968 World Sportscar Championship season">1968</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a> three times in <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1979 World Rally Championship season">1979</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 World Rally Championship season">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 World Rally Championship season">2007</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Open-wheel_car_racing">Open-wheel car racing</span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="IndyCar">IndyCar</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ArieLuyendyk1996recordcar.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/ArieLuyendyk1996recordcar.jpg/220px-ArieLuyendyk1996recordcar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/ArieLuyendyk1996recordcar.jpg/220px-ArieLuyendyk1996recordcar.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ArieLuyendyk1996recordcar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arie Luyendyk's record-setting Ford Cosworth-powered IndyCar from 1996</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/American_open-wheel_car_racing" title="American open-wheel car racing">IndyCars</a> with Ford engines first competed in 1935 using a <a href="/wiki/Ford_flathead_V8_engine" title="Ford flathead V8 engine">production-based Ford V8</a> in the Miller-Ford racer.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Overhead_valve_engine" title="Overhead valve engine">pushrod</a> Ford V8 raced with Lotus in 1963, and Ford's first Indy win was in 1965 with a <a href="/wiki/Overhead_camshaft#Dual_overhead_camshaft" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead camshaft">DOHC</a> V8.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Ford motors, including the Ford-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Cosworth_DFV#DFX" title="Cosworth DFV">DFX engine</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a>, have won the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_500" title="Indianapolis 500">Indianapolis 500</a> eighteen times.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> On May 12, 1996, <a href="/wiki/Arie_Luyendyk" title="Arie Luyendyk">Arie Luyendyk</a>, while driving an IndyCar powered by a Ford Cosworth XB engine, broke the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_500_records" title="Indianapolis 500 records">Indianapolis 500 records</a> for fastest qualification lap (237.498 mph (382.216 km/h)) and fastest qualification four-lap average (236.986 mph (381.392 km/h)).<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> These speed records still stand as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Formula_Ford">Formula Ford</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Formula_Ford" title="Formula Ford">Formula Ford</a>, conceived in the UK in 1966, is an entry-level type of <a href="/wiki/Formula_racing" title="Formula racing">formula racing</a> with wingless single-seater cars. Many of today's formula racing drivers started their car racing careers in this category.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Formula_One">Formula One</span></h4>
<p>Ford was heavily involved in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> for many years and supplied engines to a large number of teams from 1967 until 2004. These engines were designed and manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a>, the racing division that was owned by Ford from 1998 to 2004. Ford-badged engines won 176 Grands Prix between 1967 and 2003 for teams such as <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Team Lotus</a> and <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a>. Ford entered Formula One as a constructor in 2000 under the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Racing" title="Jaguar Racing">Jaguar Racing</a> name, after buying the <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Grand_Prix" title="Stewart Grand Prix">Stewart Grand Prix</a> team which had been its primary 'works' team in the series since 1997. Jaguar achieved little success in Formula One, and after a turbulent five seasons, Ford withdrew from the category after the <a href="/wiki/2004_Formula_One_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Formula One season">2004 season</a>, selling both Jaguar Racing (which became <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a>) and Cosworth (to <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Forsythe" title="Gerald Forsythe">Gerald Forsythe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Kalkhoven" title="Kevin Kalkhoven">Kevin Kalkhoven</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Stock_car_racing">Stock car racing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blaney_Heads_Off_For_Practice..jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Blaney_Heads_Off_For_Practice..jpg/220px-Blaney_Heads_Off_For_Practice..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Blaney_Heads_Off_For_Practice..jpg/220px-Blaney_Heads_Off_For_Practice..jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blaney_Heads_Off_For_Practice..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Blaney" title="Ryan Blaney">Ryan Blaney</a> driving the iconic No. 21 Wood Brothers Ford in 2016 at <a href="/wiki/Michigan_International_Speedway" title="Michigan International Speedway">Michigan International Speedway</a></div></div></div>
<p>Ford is one of three manufacturers in <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>'s three major series: the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Cup_Series" title="NASCAR Cup Series">Cup Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Xfinity_Series" title="NASCAR Xfinity Series">Xfinity Series</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Gander_RV_%26_Outdoors_Truck_Series" title="NASCAR Gander RV &amp; Outdoors Truck Series">Truck Series</a>. Major teams include <a href="/wiki/Roush_Fenway_Racing" title="Roush Fenway Racing">Roush Fenway Racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_Penske" title="Team Penske">Team Penske</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stewart-Haas_Racing" title="Stewart-Haas Racing">Stewart-Haas Racing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wood_Brothers_Racing" title="Wood Brothers Racing">Wood Brothers Racing</a>. Ford is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Mustang GT</a> in the Cup Series, and the Xfinity Series and by the <a href="/wiki/F-150" class="mw-redirect" title="F-150">F-150</a> in the Truck Series. Some of the most successful NASCAR Fords were the aerodynamic fastback <a href="/wiki/Ford_Torino" title="Ford Torino">Ford Torino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Torino_Talladega" title="Ford Torino Talladega">Ford Torino Talladega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Cyclone_Spoiler_II" title="Mercury Cyclone Spoiler II">Mercury Cyclone Spoiler II</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Montego" title="Mercury Montego">Mercury Montegos</a>, and the aero-era <a href="/wiki/Ford_Thunderbird" title="Ford Thunderbird">Ford Thunderbirds</a>. The Ford nameplate has won eight <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series#Manufacturer's_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprint Cup Series">manufacturer's championships</a> in Sprint Cup while Mercury has won one. In the Sprint Cup Series, Ford earned its 1,000th victory in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Quicken_Loans_400" title="2013 Quicken Loans 400">2013 Quicken Loans 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The Ford Fusion is also used in the <a href="/wiki/ARCA_Racing_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="ARCA Racing Series">ARCA Racing Series</a>. Ford had last won a drivers' championship in the Cup Series with <a href="/wiki/Joey_Logano" title="Joey Logano">Joey Logano</a> in 2018.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Rally">Rally</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg/220px-Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg/220px-Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jari-Matti_Latvala" title="Jari-Matti Latvala">Jari-Matti Latvala</a> driving the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_RS_WRC_09" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus RS WRC 09">Ford Focus RS WRC 09</a> in 2010</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_World_Rally_Team" title="Ford World Rally Team">Ford World Rally Team</a></div>
<p>Ford has a long history in <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rallying</a> and has been active in the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a> since the beginning of the world championship, the <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1973 World Rally Championship season">1973 season</a>. Ford took the <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1979 World Rally Championship season">1979</a> manufacturers' title with <a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Waldeg%C3%A5rd" title="Björn Waldegård">Björn Waldegård</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ari_Vatanen" title="Ari Vatanen">Ari Vatanen</a> driving the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_RS1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escort RS1800">Ford Escort RS1800</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> era, Ford achieved success with <a href="/wiki/Ford_RS200" title="Ford RS200">Ford RS200</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 World Rally Championship season">1999 season</a>, Ford has used various versions of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_WRC" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus WRC">Ford Focus WRC</a> to much success. In the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 World Rally Championship season">2006 season</a>, <a href="/wiki/BP-Ford_World_Rally_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="BP-Ford World Rally Team">BP-Ford World Rally Team</a> secured Ford its second manufacturers' title, with the Focus RS WRC 06 built by <a href="/wiki/M-Sport" title="M-Sport">M-Sport</a> and driven by "<a href="/wiki/Flying_Finns" class="mw-redirect" title="Flying Finns">Flying Finns</a>" <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Grönholm">Marcus Grönholm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikko_Hirvonen" title="Mikko Hirvonen">Mikko Hirvonen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Continuing with Grönholm and Hirvonen, Ford successfully defended the manufacturers' world championship in the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 World Rally Championship season">2007 season</a>. Ford is the only manufacturer to score in the points for 92 consecutive races; since the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2002 World Rally Championship season">2002 season</a> opener <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo Rally</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Rallycross">Rallycross</span></h3>
<p>Ford has competed in rallycross with its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Ford Focus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tanner_Foust" title="Tanner Foust">Tanner Foust</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Global_RallyCross_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Global RallyCross Championship">Global RallyCross Championship</a> in 2011 and 2012 and was runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/FIA_European_Rallycross_Championship" title="FIA European Rallycross Championship">FIA European Rallycross Championship</a> in 2011 and 2012. <a href="/wiki/Toomas_Heikkinen" title="Toomas Heikkinen">Toomas Heikkinen</a> won the Global RallyCross Championship title in 2013 and <a href="/wiki/Joni_Wiman" title="Joni Wiman">Joni Wiman</a> won it in 2014. Other notable Ford drivers include <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Grönholm">Marcus Grönholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Block" title="Ken Block">Ken Block</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Deegan_(rider)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brian Deegan (rider)">Brian Deegan</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_cars">Sports cars</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT#Racing" title="Ford GT">Ford GT § Racing</a></div>
<p>Ford sports cars have been visible in the world of sports car racing since 1964. Most notably the <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT40" title="Ford GT40">GT40</a> won the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> four times in the 1960s and is the only American car to ever win overall at this prestigious event. Ford also won the <a href="/wiki/1968_World_Sportscar_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1968 World Sportscar Championship season">1968 International Championship for Makes</a> with the GT40, which still stands today as one of the all-time greatest racing cars. Swiss team <a href="/wiki/Matech_Concepts" title="Matech Concepts">Matech GT Racing</a>, in collaboration with Ford Racing, opened a new chapter with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT" title="Ford GT">Ford GT</a>, winning the Teams title in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/FIA_GT3_European_Championship" title="FIA GT3 European Championship">FIA GT3 European Championship</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbers02.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Barbers02.jpg/220px-Barbers02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Barbers02.jpg/220px-Barbers02.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbers02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A GT racing version of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a>, competing in the <a href="/wiki/IMSA_Continental_Tire_Sports_Car_Challenge" class="mw-redirect" title="IMSA Continental Tire Sports Car Challenge">Koni Challenge</a> in 2005</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang#Racing" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang § Racing</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a> has arguably been Ford's most successful sports car. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Titus" title="Jerry Titus">Jerry Titus</a> won the 1965 SCCA Pro B National Championship with a Mustang and the model went on to earn Ford the SCCA <a href="/wiki/Trans-Am_Series" title="Trans-Am Series">Trans-Am Championship</a> title in both 1966 and 1967. Ford won the Trans-Am Championship again in 1970 with <a href="/wiki/Parnelli_Jones" title="Parnelli Jones">Parnelli Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Follmer" title="George Follmer">George Follmer</a> driving <a href="/wiki/Boss_302_Mustang" title="Boss 302 Mustang">Boss 302 Mustangs</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bud_Moore_Engineering" title="Bud Moore Engineering">Bud Moore Engineering</a>. Ford took the 1985 and 1986 <a href="/wiki/IMSA_GT_Championship" title="IMSA GT Championship">IMSA GTO Championship</a> with Mustangs driven by <a href="/wiki/John_Jones_(racing_driver)" title="John Jones (racing driver)">John Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pruett" title="Scott Pruett">Scott Pruett</a> before returning to Trans-Am glory with a championship in 1989 with <a href="/wiki/Dorsey_Schroeder" title="Dorsey Schroeder">Dorsey Schroeder</a>. Ford dominated Trans-Am in the 1990s with <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Kendall" title="Tommy Kendall">Tommy Kendall</a> winning championships in 1993, 1995, 1996, and 1997 with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gentilozzi" title="Paul Gentilozzi">Paul Gentilozzi</a> adding yet another title in 1999. In 2005 the Ford Mustang FR500C took the championship in the Rolex <a href="/wiki/IMSA_Continental_Tire_Sports_Car_Challenge" class="mw-redirect" title="IMSA Continental Tire Sports Car Challenge">Koni Challenge</a> Series in its first year on the circuit. In 2007, Ford added a victory in the GT4 European Championship. 2008 was the first year of the Mustang Challenge for the Miller Cup, a series which pits a full field of identical factory-built Ford Mustang race cars against each other. Also, in 2008, Ford won the manufacturers championship in the <a href="/wiki/IMSA_Continental_Tire_Sports_Car_Challenge" class="mw-redirect" title="IMSA Continental Tire Sports Car Challenge">Koni Challenge</a> Series and HyperSport drivers Joe Foster and Steve Maxwell won the drivers title in a Mustang GT.
</p><p>Ford and <a href="/wiki/Michelin" title="Michelin">Michelin</a> teamed up to provide custom-engineered tires for the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance" title="Ford Performance">Ford Performance</a> vehicle lineup. <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance" title="Ford Performance">Ford Performance</a> director Dave Pericak said: "That confidence extends from our upcoming racing effort at Le Mans in 2016 with the all-new <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT" title="Ford GT">Ford GT</a>, to the Ford Performance vehicle lineup, including the <a href="/wiki/Shelby_GT350" class="mw-redirect" title="Shelby GT350">Shelby GT350</a> and F-150 Raptor".<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Touring_cars">Touring cars</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winterbottom2008.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Winterbottom2008.jpg/220px-Winterbottom2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="755" data-file-height="452"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 132px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Winterbottom2008.jpg/220px-Winterbottom2008.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="132" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winterbottom2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Performance Racing">Ford Performance Racing</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Ford Falcon</a> <a href="/wiki/V8_Supercar" class="mw-redirect" title="V8 Supercar">V8 Supercar</a> at Eastern Creek in Australia in 2008</div></div></div>
<p>Ford has campaigned touring cars such as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus (international)">Focus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Falcon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Contour" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Contour">Contour</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Sierra</a> <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a> in many different series throughout the years. Notably, Mondeo drivers finished 1,2,3 in the 2000 <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">British Touring Car Championship</a> and Falcon drivers placed 1,2,3 in the <a href="/wiki/2005_V8_Supercar_Championship_Series" title="2005 V8 Supercar Championship Series">2005 V8 Supercar Championship Series</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Drag_racing">Drag racing</span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Drag_racing" title="Drag racing">drag racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Force_Racing" title="John Force Racing">John Force Racing</a> drivers <a href="/wiki/John_Force" title="John Force">John Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Pedregon" title="Tony Pedregon">Tony Pedregon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hight" title="Robert Hight">Robert Hight</a> have piloted <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a> <a href="/wiki/Funny_Car" title="Funny Car">Funny Cars</a> to several <a href="/wiki/National_Hot_Rod_Association" title="National Hot Rod Association">NHRA</a> titles in recent seasons. Teammates <a href="/wiki/Tim_Wilkerson" title="Tim Wilkerson">Tim Wilkerson</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bob_Tasca_III&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bob Tasca III (page does not exist)">Bob Tasca III</a> also drive Mustangs in Funny Car.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Drifting">Drifting</span></h3>
<p>Ford has branched out into <a href="/wiki/Drifting_(motorsport)" title="Drifting (motorsport)">drifting</a> with the introduction of the new model Mustang. Most noticeable is the Turquoise and Blue Falken Tires Mustang driven by <a href="/wiki/Vaughn_Gittin,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Vaughn Gittin, Jr.">Vaughn Gittin, Jr.</a>, (A.K.A. "JR") that produces 750 RWHP (Rear Wheel Horsepower).
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_initiatives">Environmental initiatives</span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Compressed_natural_gas">Compressed natural gas</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fossil_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative fossil fuel">alternative fossil fuel</a> vehicles, such as some versions of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Victoria" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Victoria">Crown Victoria</a> especially in fleet and taxi service, operate on <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">compressed natural gas</a>—or CNG. Some CNG vehicles have dual fuel tanks – one for gasoline, the other for CNG – the same engine can operate on either fuel via a selector switch.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Flexible_fuel_vehicles">Flexible fuel vehicles</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Focus_Flexifuel_in_Madrid_with_flexifuel_badging.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ford_Focus_Flexifuel_in_Madrid_with_flexifuel_badging.jpg/220px-Ford_Focus_Flexifuel_in_Madrid_with_flexifuel_badging.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2661" data-file-height="1774"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ford_Focus_Flexifuel_in_Madrid_with_flexifuel_badging.jpg/220px-Ford_Focus_Flexifuel_in_Madrid_with_flexifuel_badging.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Focus_Flexifuel_in_Madrid_with_flexifuel_badging.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ford Focus Flexifuel was the first <a href="/wiki/Common_ethanol_fuel_mixtures#E85" title="Common ethanol fuel mixtures">E85</a> <a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Flexible fuel vehicle">flexible fuel vehicle</a> commercially available in the European market.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Flexible fuel vehicle">Flexible fuel vehicles</a> are designed to operate smoothly using a wide range of available <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol fuel</a> mixtures—from pure gasoline to <a href="/wiki/Bioethanol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bioethanol">bioethanol</a>-gasoline blends such as <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> (85% <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a> and 15% gasoline) or <a href="/wiki/Common_ethanol_fuel_mixtures" title="Common ethanol fuel mixtures">E100</a> (neat <a href="/wiki/Hydrous" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrous">hydrous</a> ethanol) in Brazil. Part of the challenge of successful marketing alternative and flexible fuel vehicles in the U.S. is the general lack of establishment of sufficient <a href="/wiki/Fueling_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fueling station">fueling stations</a>, which would be essential for these vehicles to be attractive to a wide range of consumers. Significant efforts to ramp up production and distribution of <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> fuels are underway and expanding.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Current Ford E100 Flex sold in the Brazilian market are the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Courier" title="Ford Courier">Courier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_EcoSport" title="Ford EcoSport">Ford EcoSport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus (international)">Ford Focus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ka" title="Ford Ka">Ford Ka</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_drive_vehicles">Electric drive vehicles</span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_electric_vehicles">Hybrid electric vehicles</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Escape_plug-in_hybrid.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ford_Escape_plug-in_hybrid.jpg/220px-Ford_Escape_plug-in_hybrid.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2008" data-file-height="1296"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 142px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ford_Escape_plug-in_hybrid.jpg/220px-Ford_Escape_plug-in_hybrid.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="142" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Escape_plug-in_hybrid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape" title="Ford Escape">Ford Escape</a> <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> test vehicle</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Bush_visit_Kansas_City_Assembly.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/George_Bush_visit_Kansas_City_Assembly.jpg/220px-George_Bush_visit_Kansas_City_Assembly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="369"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 158px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/George_Bush_visit_Kansas_City_Assembly.jpg/220px-George_Bush_visit_Kansas_City_Assembly.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="158" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Bush_visit_Kansas_City_Assembly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mulally (second from left) with then-President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Assembly">Kansas City Assembly</a> plant in <a href="/wiki/Claycomo,_Missouri" title="Claycomo, Missouri">Claycomo</a>, Missouri on March 20, 2007, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/touting" class="extiw" title="wikt:touting">touting</a> Ford's new hybrid cars</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">Hybrid electric vehicle</a></div>
<p>In 2004, Ford and Toyota agreed a patent sharing accord which granted Ford access to certain hybrid technology patented by Toyota; in exchange, Ford licensed Toyota some of its own patents.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> In 2004, Ford introduced the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escape Hybrid">Escape Hybrid</a>. With this vehicle, Ford was third to the automotive market with a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid electric vehicle</a> and the first hybrid electric <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> to market. This was also the first hybrid electric vehicle with a <a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Flexible fuel">flexible fuel</a> capability to run on <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The Escape's platform mate <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Mariner" title="Mercury Mariner">Mercury Mariner</a> was also available with the hybrid-electric system in the 2006 model year—a full year ahead of schedule. The similar <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Tribute" title="Mazda Tribute">Mazda Tribute</a> will also receive a hybrid-electric powertrain option, along with many other vehicles in the Ford vehicle line.
</p><p>In 2005, Ford announced a goal to make 250,000 hybrids a year by 2010, but by mid-2006 announced that it would not meet that goal, due to excessively high costs and the lack of sufficient supplies of the hybrid-electric batteries and drivetrain system components.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Instead, Ford has committed to accelerating development of next-generation hybrid-electric power plants in Britain, in collaboration with Volvo. This engineering study is expected to yield more than 100 new hybrid-electric vehicle models and derivatives.
</p><p>In September 2007, Ford announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Edison" title="Southern California Edison">Southern California Edison</a> (SCE) to examine how <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> will work with the electrical grid. Under the multimillion-dollar, multi-year project, Ford will convert a demonstration fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escape Hybrid">Ford Escape Hybrids</a> into plug-in hybrids, and SCE will evaluate how the vehicles might interact with the home and the utility's electrical grid. Some of the vehicles will be evaluated "in typical customer settings", according to Ford.<sup id="cite_ref-akhrum_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhrum-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-edison_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edison-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>On June 12, 2008, <a href="/wiki/USDOE" class="mw-redirect" title="USDOE">USDOE</a> expanded its own fleet of alternative fuel and advanced technology vehicles with the addition of a Ford Escape Plug-In Hybrid Flex-Fuel Vehicle. The vehicle is equipped with a 10-kilowatt (13 hp) <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium-ion">lithium-ion</a> battery supplied by <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls-Saft" class="mw-redirect" title="Johnson Controls-Saft">Johnson Controls-Saft</a> that stores enough electric energy to drive up to 30 miles (48 km) at speeds of up to 40 mph (64 km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> In March 2009, Ford launched hybrid versions of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Milan_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercury Milan Hybrid">Mercury Milan Hybrid</a> in the United States, both as 2010 models.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenCar0409_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenCar0409-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>As of November 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Ford has produced for retail sales the following hybrid electric vehicles: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escape Hybrid">Ford Escape Hybrid</a> (2004–2012), <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Mariner#Hybrid" title="Mercury Mariner">Mercury Mariner Hybrid</a> (2005–2010), <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Milan_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercury Milan Hybrid">Mercury Milan Hybrid</a> (2009–2010), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a> (2009–present), <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKZ_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln MKZ Hybrid">Lincoln MKZ Hybrid</a> (2010–present), <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford C-Max Hybrid">Ford C-Max Hybrid</a> (2012–present), and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo_Hybrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Mondeo Hybrid">Ford Mondeo Hybrid</a> (2014–present). By June 2012, Ford had sold 200,000 full hybrids in the US since 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-Ford200K_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ford200K-164">[164]</a></sup> and, as of September 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the carmaker has sold over 344 thousand hybrids in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Ford200K_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ford200K-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales092014US_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales092014US-167">[167]</a></sup> The top selling hybrids in the U.S. market are the Fusion Hybrid with 127,572 units, followed by Escape Hybrid with 117,997 units, and the C-Max Hybrid with 54,236.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales092014US_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales092014US-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DoEHEV10_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV10-169">[169]</a></sup> As of November 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Ford is the world's second largest manufacturer of hybrids after <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Toyota Motor Corporation">Toyota Motor Corporation</a>, with 400,000 hybrid electric vehicles produced since their introduction in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Plug-in_electric_vehicles">Plug-in electric vehicles</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">Plug-in electric vehicle</a></div>
<p>As of October 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Ford has produced the following <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicles</a>: the all-electric <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger_EV" title="Ford Ranger EV">Ford Ranger EV</a> (1997–2002), <a href="/wiki/Ford_TH!NK" title="Ford TH!NK">Ford TH!NK</a> (1999–2003), <a href="/wiki/Azure_Transit_Connect_Electric" title="Azure Transit Connect Electric">Transit Connect</a> (2010–2012), and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_Electric" title="Ford Focus Electric">Ford Focus Electric</a> (December 2011–present); and the <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Energi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford C-Max Energi">C-MAX Energi</a> (October 2012–present) and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Energi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Fusion Energi">Fusion Energi</a> (February 2013–present), sold under the Mondeo nameplate in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-autoblog_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autoblog-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-energy1_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-energy1-172">[172]</a></sup> Since the launch of the Focus Electric in 2011, combined sales of all Ford <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric models</a> amounted to just over 56,000 through October 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Transit_Connect_EV_EDTA_DC_04_2011_1806.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Transit_Connect_EV_EDTA_DC_04_2011_1806.jpg/220px-Transit_Connect_EV_EDTA_DC_04_2011_1806.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Transit_Connect_EV_EDTA_DC_04_2011_1806.jpg/220px-Transit_Connect_EV_EDTA_DC_04_2011_1806.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Transit_Connect_EV_EDTA_DC_04_2011_1806.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Azure_Transit_Connect_Electric" title="Azure Transit Connect Electric">Azure Transit Connect Electric</a> was produced between 2010 and 2012 as a collaboration between <a href="/wiki/Azure_Dynamics" title="Azure Dynamics">Azure Dynamics</a> and Ford Motor Company.</div></div></div>
<p>Bill Ford was one of the first top industry executives to make regular use of a <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicle</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger_EV" title="Ford Ranger EV">Ford Ranger EV</a>, while the company contracted with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> to deliver electric postal vans based on the Ranger EV platform. Ford discontinued a line of electric <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger" title="Ford Ranger">Ranger</a> <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickup trucks</a> and ordered them destroyed, though it reversed in January 2005, after environmentalist protest.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> The all-electric pickup truck leased 205 units to individuals and 1,500 units to fleets in the U.S. from 1998 to 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Rand02_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rand02-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boschert06_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boschert06-176">[176]</a></sup></p><p>From 2009 to 2011, Ford offered the <a href="/wiki/Ford_TH!NK" title="Ford TH!NK">Ford TH!NK</a> car. Ford ended production and ordered all the cars repossessed and destroyed, even as many of the people leasing them begged to be able to buy the cars from Ford. After outcry from the lessees and activists in the US and Norway, Ford returned the cars to Norway for sale.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> 440 units were leased in the U.S. from 1999 until 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Boschert06_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boschert06-176">[176]</a></sup></p><p>In 2017, CEO of Ford <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a> announced that the company will invest $4.5 billion in further development of plug-in electric vehicles by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Azure_Transit_Connect_Electric" title="Azure Transit Connect Electric">Azure Transit Connect Electric</a> was an <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">all-electric</a> <a href="/wiki/Van" title="Van">van</a> developed as a collaboration between <a href="/wiki/Azure_Dynamics" title="Azure Dynamics">Azure Dynamics</a> and Ford Motor Company, but Azure was the official manufacturer of record.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ0910_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ0910-179">[179]</a></sup> The Transit Connect Electric had an official <a href="/wiki/US_Environmental_Protection_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="US Environmental Protection Agency">US Environmental Protection Agency</a> all-electric range of 56 mi (90 km).<sup id="cite_ref-EPATransitEV_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPATransitEV-180">[180]</a></sup> The EPA rated the combined city/highway <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy</a> at 62 <a href="/wiki/Miles_per_gallon_gasoline_equivalent" title="Miles per gallon gasoline equivalent">miles per gallon gasoline equivalent</a> (3.8 L/100 km equivalent).<sup id="cite_ref-EPATransitEV_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPATransitEV-180">[180]</a></sup> Deliveries for fleet customers in the U.S. and Canada began in December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1207_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1207-181">[181]</a></sup> Production of the electric van was stopped in March 2012 as a result of Azure's bankruptcy protection filing. Ford continues to provide servicing.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Around 500 units were sold before Azure stopped production.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Fusion_Energi_SEL_with_badge_WAS_2012_0583.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Ford_Fusion_Energi_SEL_with_badge_WAS_2012_0583.jpg/220px-Ford_Fusion_Energi_SEL_with_badge_WAS_2012_0583.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3731" data-file-height="2000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 118px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Ford_Fusion_Energi_SEL_with_badge_WAS_2012_0583.jpg/220px-Ford_Fusion_Energi_SEL_with_badge_WAS_2012_0583.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="118" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Fusion_Energi_SEL_with_badge_WAS_2012_0583.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Energi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Fusion Energi">Ford Fusion Energi</a> <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> shares its powertrain with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Energi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford C-Max Energi">Ford C-Max Energi</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_Electric" title="Ford Focus Electric">Ford Focus Electric</a> is based on the next generation <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(North_America)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus (North America)">Focus</a> internal combustion vehicle, converted to an <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">all-electric</a> propulsion system as a production <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric car</a> by Magna International, and retail sales began in the U.S. in December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The Focus Electric has an EPA rated range of 76 mi (122 km) and a combined city/highway fuel economy of 105 <a href="/wiki/Miles_per_gallon_gasoline_equivalent" title="Miles per gallon gasoline equivalent">miles per gallon gasoline equivalent</a> (2.2 L/100 km).<sup id="cite_ref-EPAFocusEV_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAFocusEV-186">[186]</a></sup> Available also in Canada and several European countries, 3,965 units have been sold in the U.S. through September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_165-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales092014US_167-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales092014US-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FocusBEV122011_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FocusBEV122011-187">[187]</a></sup></p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Energi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford C-Max Energi">Ford C-Max Energi</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> released in the U.S. in October 2012. The C-Max Energi has an EPA rated <a href="/wiki/All-electric_range" title="All-electric range">all-electric range</a> of 20 mi (32 km) and a combined city/highway fuel economy in <a href="/wiki/All-electric_mode" class="mw-redirect" title="All-electric mode">all-electric mode</a> at 88 <a href="/wiki/Miles_per_gallon_of_gasoline_equivalent" class="mw-redirect" title="Miles per gallon of gasoline equivalent">MPG-e</a> (2.7 L/100 km).<sup id="cite_ref-Energi2013_14_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energi2013_14-188">[188]</a></sup> U.S. sales totaled 33,509 units
through December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_165-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_166-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2015US_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2015US-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2016US_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2016US-191">[191]</a></sup> Deliveries of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Energi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Fusion Energi">Ford Fusion Energi</a> began in the United States in February 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-EnergiDelivery01_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnergiDelivery01-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EnergiDelivery02_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnergiDelivery02-193">[193]</a></sup> The Fusion Energi has an all-electric range of 20 mi (32 km) and an equivalent fuel economy EPA rating of 88 MPG-e (2.7 L/100 km).<sup id="cite_ref-Energi2013_14_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energi2013_14-188">[188]</a></sup> As of December 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ford_Motor_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 43,327 units have been delivered in the U.S. since its inception.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_166-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2015US_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2015US-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2016US_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2016US-191">[191]</a></sup></p><p>Both Energi models share the same powertrain technology and have the same EPA combined city/highway fuel economy in <a href="/wiki/Charge-sustaining" class="mw-redirect" title="Charge-sustaining">hybrid</a> operation of 38 mpg<sub>‑US</sub> (6.2 L/100 km; 46 mpg<sub>‑imp</sub>).<sup id="cite_ref-Energi2013_14_188-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energi2013_14-188">[188]</a></sup>
When asked about a battery-electric vehicle with a 200-mile (320 km) range, Fields said in April 2016 "Clearly that's something we're developing for". Ford has a pending trademark application on the "Model E" name,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> preventing the <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_3" title="Tesla Model 3">Tesla Model 3</a> in using the name.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2017, Ford announced its Team Edison battery-electric vehicle group to lead the company's renewed efforts into the EV market, in which it currently offers only the Focus subcompact and has plans for a small 300-mile SUV by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The new team will be headquartered in Detroit and have offices in Europe and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrogen">Hydrogen</span></h3>
<p>Ford also continues to study <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a>-powered electric powertrains and has demonstrated hydrogen-fueled <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> technologies, as well as developing the next-generation hybrid-electric systems. Compared with conventional vehicles, <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid vehicles</a> and/or fuel cell vehicles decrease air pollution emissions as well as sound levels, with favorable impacts upon respiratory health and decrease of <a href="/wiki/Noise_health_effects" class="mw-redirect" title="Noise health effects">noise health effects</a>.
</p><p>Ford has launched the production of <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle" title="Hydrogen vehicle">hydrogen-powered</a> shuttle buses, using hydrogen instead of gasoline in a standard <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle#Hydrogen_internal_combustion" title="Hydrogen vehicle">internal combustion engine</a>, for use at airports and convention centers.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> At the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Auto_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Los Angeles Auto Show">Greater Los Angeles Auto Show</a>, Ford showcased a hydrogen fuel cell version of its Explorer SUV. The Fuel cell Explorer has a combined output of 174 hp (130 kW). It has a large hydrogen storage tank which is situated in the center of the car taking the original place of the conventional model's automatic transmission. The centered position of the tank assists the vehicle reach a notable range of 350 miles (563 km), the farthest for a fuel cell vehicle so far. The fuel cell Explorer the first in a series of prototypes partly funded by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">United States Department of Energy</a> to expand efforts to determine the feasibility of hydrogen- powered vehicles. The fuel cell Explorer is one of several vehicles with green technology being featured at the L.A. show, including the 2008 Ford Escape Hybrid, PZEV emissions compliant Fusion and Focus models and a 2008 Ford F-Series Super Duty outfitted with Ford's clean diesel technology.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Increased_fuel_efficiency">Increased fuel efficiency</span></h3>
<p>Ford Motor Company announced it will accelerate its plans to produce more fuel-efficient cars, changing both its North American manufacturing plans and its lineup of vehicles available in the United States. In terms of North American manufacturing, the company will convert three existing truck and sport utility vehicle (SUV) plants for small car production, with the first conversion at its Michigan Truck Plant. In addition, Ford's assembly plants near Mexico City, Mexico, and in Louisville, Kentucky, will convert from pickups and SUVs to small cars, including the Ford Fiesta, by 2011. Ford will also introduce to North America six of its European small vehicles, including two versions of the Ford Fiesta, by the end of 2012.
</p><p>Ford of Europe developed the <a href="/wiki/ECOnetic" title="ECOnetic">ECOnetic</a> programme to address the market and legislative need for higher fuel efficiency and lower CO2 emissions. As opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid engine">hybrid engine</a> technology used in competitor products such as the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a>, ECOnetic improves existing technology. Using lower consuming <a href="/wiki/Ford_Duratorq_engine" title="Ford Duratorq engine">Duratorq TDCi</a> diesel engines, and based on a combination of improved aerodynamics, lower resistance, and improved efficiency, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a> is currently the lowest emitting mass-produced car in Europe<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Focus (international)">2012 Ford Focus ECOnetic</a> will have better fuel consumption than the Prius or the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Volkswagen Golf</a> <a href="/wiki/BlueMotion" title="BlueMotion">BlueMotion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> ECOnetic is not presently planned to be sold in North American due to current perceived lower consumer demand.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p><p>Ford has challenged University teams to create a vehicle that is simple, durable, lightweight, and come equipped with a base target price of only $7,000. The students from <a href="/wiki/Aachen_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Aachen University">Aachen University</a> created the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Ford_Model_T&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2015 Ford Model T (page does not exist)">2015 Ford Model T</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p><p>In 2000, under the leadership of the current Ford chairman, William Clay Ford, the company announced<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> a planned 25 percent improvement in the average mileage of its <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUVs</a> – to be completed by the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Calendar_year" title="Calendar year">calendar year</a>. In 2003, Ford announced that competitive market conditions and technological and cost challenges would prevent the company from achieving this goal.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p><p>For the 2007 model year, Ford had thirteen U.S. models that achieve 30 miles per gallon or better (based on the highway fuel economy estimates of the EPA) and several of Ford's vehicles were recognized in the EPA and Department of Energy Fuel Economy Guide for best-in-class fuel economy. Ford claimed to have eliminated nearly three million pounds of smog-forming emissions from their U.S. cars and light trucks over the 2004 to 2006 model years.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> However, the United States Environmental Protection Agency has linked Ford to 54 <a href="/wiki/Superfund" title="Superfund">Superfund</a> toxic waste sites, twelve of which have been cleaned up and deleted from the list.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="PC_power_management">PC power management</span></h3>
<p>In March 2010, Ford announced its <a href="/wiki/PC_power_management" title="PC power management">PC power management</a> system which it developed with NightWatchman software from <a href="/wiki/1E" title="1E">1E</a>. The company is expected to save $1.2m on power cost and reduce carbon footprint by an estimated 16,000 to 25,000 metric tons annually when the system is fully implemented.
</p><p>According to company, reduction in carbon footprint and power cost will be achieved by developing 'Power Profiles' for every PC in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>Ford sponsors numerous events and sports facilities around the US, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Center_(Evansville)" title="Ford Center (Evansville)">Ford Center</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Evansville,_Indiana" title="Evansville, Indiana">Evansville, Indiana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Field" title="Ford Field">Ford Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Detroit" title="Downtown Detroit">downtown Detroit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p><p>Ford has also been a major sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> for over two decades and is also a longtime sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/Sky_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky plc">Sky media channel's</a> coverage of <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> football. Senior Ford marketer Mark Jones explained in May 2013 the process behind the two sponsorship deals:
</p>
<blockquote><p>
We start with a blank piece of paper and work out if the sponsorship still works for us and ask does it meet our objectives? We want to find a moment in time when people come together and have a collective experience and we achieve this through the sponsorships.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
